## Domain Knowledge (LLM-generated)
**Domain**: nonlinear dynamics / classical mechanics
**Analysis**: This task models the acceleration of a nonlinear harmonic oscillator, where dv_dt depends on position x (restoring force), velocity v (damping), and possibly time t (external driving). The nonlinearity can appear in restoring forces, damping, or both.

**Common formula structures in this domain**:
- Simple harmonic oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x (linear restoring force)
- Damped harmonic oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v (linear restoring + linear damping)
- Duffing oscillator (unforced): dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 (cubic nonlinear restoring force)
- Damped Duffing oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * v (cubic restoring + linear damping)
- Driven Duffing oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * v + c3 * cos(c4 * t) (forced nonlinear oscillator)
- Van der Pol oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * (c1 + c2 * x**2) * v + c3 * x (nonlinear damping)
- Quintic nonlinear oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * x**5 (higher-order restoring force)
- Duffing with quadratic term: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**2 + c2 * x**3 (asymmetric potential)
- Parametrically driven oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x * cos(c1 * t) + c2 * v (time-modulated stiffness)
- Nonlinear damping with driving: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * v * x**2 + c3 * sin(c4 * t)
- Helmholtz oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**2 + c2 * v (quadratic nonlinearity with damping)
- Rayleigh oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v + c2 * v**3 (cubic velocity damping)
- General polynomial restoring + damping: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * v + c3 * v**3 + c4 * cos(c5 * t)
- Coulomb-like friction oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v * (c2 + v**2)**(-0.5) (velocity-dependent friction)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope ŌåÆ Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects ŌåÆ Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay ŌåÆ Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior ŌåÆ Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects ŌåÆ Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Odd-power restoring forces (x, x**3, x**5) preserve symmetry of the potential well; even powers (x**2) break symmetry
- Velocity-dependent terms proportional to v represent energy dissipation or injection (damping/anti-damping)
- Products of x**2 and v (e.g., x**2 * v) indicate amplitude-dependent damping characteristic of van der Pol-type systems
- Periodic time dependence via sin(c*t) or cos(c*t) indicates external forcing, which can lead to resonance and chaos
- Negative linear stiffness (positive coefficient on x when dv_dt = ... + c*x with c>0 meaning away from origin) combined with cubic restoring creates double-well potentials
- Odd-order velocity terms (v**3) model nonlinear drag forces like aerodynamic resistance
- Time appearing only inside trigonometric functions suggests autonomous dynamics with periodic driving rather than explicit time dependence of parameters
- Ratio of cubic to linear restoring force coefficients determines whether the oscillator is hardening (same sign) or softening (opposite sign)
